# Kubernetes API Server Admission Controller Chain

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the API server admission controller pipeline: the admission.Interface registration, the generic admission chain execution, the mutating admission ordering, and the validating admission webhook call.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

    29→// Attributes is an interface used by AdmissionController to get information about a request
    30→// that is used to make an admission decision.
    31→type Attributes interface {
    32→	// GetName returns the name of the object as presented in the request.  On a CREATE operation, the client
    33→	// may omit name and rely on the server to generate the name.  If that is the case, this method will return
    34→	// the empty string
    35→	GetName() string
    36→	// GetNamespace is the namespace associated with the request (if any)
    37→	GetNamespace() string
    38→	// GetResource is the name of the resource being requested.  This is not the kind.  For example: pods
    39→	GetResource() schema.GroupVersionResource
    40→	// GetSubresource is the name of the subresource being requested. 
... (truncated)

    17→package admission
    18→
    19→import "context"
    20→
    21→// chainAdmissionHandler is an instance of admission.NamedHandler that performs admission control using
    22→// a chain of admission handlers
    23→type chainAdmissionHandler []Interface
    24→
    25→// NewChainHandler creates a new chain handler from an array of handlers. Used for testing.
    26→func NewChainHandler(handlers ...Interface) chainAdmissionHandler {
    27→	return chainAdmissionHandler(handlers)
    28→}
    29→
    30→// Admit performs an admission control check using a chain of handlers, and returns immediately on first error
    31→func (admissionHandler chainAdmissionHandler) Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error {
    32→	for _, handler := range admissionHandler {
    33→		if !handler.Handles(a.GetOperation()) {
    34→			continue
    35→		}
    36→		if mutator, ok := handler.(MutationInterface); ok {
    37→			err := mutator.Admit(ctx, a, o)
    38→			if err != nil {
    39→				return err
    40→			}
    41→		}
    42→	}
    43→	return nil
    44→}
    45→

    18→
    19→import (
    20→	"os"
    21→

    23→
    24→	"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission"
    25→)
    26→
    27→// Config holds the configuration needed to for initialize the admission plugins
    28→type Config struct {
    29→	CloudConfigFile string
    30→}
    31→
    32→// New sets up the plugins and admission start hooks needed for admission
    33→func (c *Config) New() ([]admission.PluginInitializer, error) {
    34→	var cloudConfig []byte
    35→	if c.CloudConfigFile != "" {
    36→		var err error
    37→		cloudConfig, err = os.ReadFile(c.CloudConfigFile)
    38→		if err != nil {
    39→			klog.Fatalf("Error reading from cloud configuration file %s: %#v", c.CloudConfigFile, err)
    40→		}
    41→	}
    42→
    43→	return []admission.PluginInitializer{NewPluginInitializer(cloudConfig)}, nil
    44→}

    17→package admission
    18→
    19→import "context"
    20→
    21→// chainAdmissionHandler is an instance of admission.NamedHandler that performs admission control using
    22→// a chain of admission handlers
    23→type chainAdmissionHandler []Interface
    24→
    25→// NewChainHandler creates a new chain handler from an array of handlers. Used for testing.
    26→func NewChainHandler(handlers ...Interface) chainAdmissionHandler {
    27→	return chainAdmissionHandler(handlers)
    28→}
    29→
    30→// Admit performs an admission control check using a chain of handlers, and returns immediately on first error
    31→func (admissionHandler chainAdmissionHandler) Admit(ctx context.Context, a Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error {
    32→	for _, handler := range admissionHandler {
    33→		if !handler.Handles(a.GetOperation()) {
    34→			continue
    35→		}
    36→		if mutator, ok := handler.(MutationInterface); ok {
    37→			err := mutator.Admit(ctx, a, o)
    38→			if err != nil {
    39→				return err
    40→			}
    41→		}
    42→	}
    43→	return nil
    44→}
    45→
    46→// Validate

    33→// the admission attributes' reinvocation context against their reinvocation policy to decide if
    34→// they should re-run, and to update the reinvocation context if they perform any mutations.

    36→	if mutator, ok := r.admissionChain.(MutationInterface); ok {

   184→// NamespaceScopedStrategy has a method to tell if the object must be in a namespace.

   190→// AdmissionToValidateObjectFunc converts validating admission to a rest validate object func
   191→func AdmissionToValidateObjectFunc(admit admission.Interface, staticAttributes admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) ValidateObjectFunc {
   192→	validatingAdmission, ok := admit.(admission.ValidationInterface)
   193→	if !ok {
   194→		return func(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object) error { return nil }
   195→	}
   196→	return func(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object) error {
   197→		name := staticAttributes.GetName()
   198→		// in case the generated name is populated
   199→		if len(name) == 0 {
   200→			if metadata, err := meta.Accessor(obj); err == nil {
   201→				name = metadata.GetName()
   202→			}
   203→		}
   204→
   205→		finalAttributes := admission.NewAttributesRecord(
   206→			obj,
   207→			staticAttributes.GetOldObject(),
   208→			staticAttributes.GetKind(),
   209→			staticAttributes.GetNamespace(),
   210→			name,
   211→			staticAttributes.GetResource(),
   212→			staticAttributes.GetSubresource(),
   213→			staticAttributes.GetOperation(),
   214→			staticAttributes.GetOperationOptions(),
   215→			staticAttributes.IsDryRun(),
   216→			staticAttributes.GetUserInfo(),
   217→		)
   218→		if !validatingAdmission.Handles(finalAttributes.GetOperation()) {
   219→			return nil
   220→		}
   221→		return validatingAdmission.Validate(ctx, finalAttributes, o)
   222→	}
   223→}

    35→// WithAudit is a decorator for a admission phase. It saves annotations
    36→// of attribute into the audit event. Attributes passed to the Admit and
    37→// Validate function must be instance of privateAnnotationsGetter or
    38→// AnnotationsGetter, otherwise an error is returned.
    39→func WithAudit(i Interface) Interface {
    40→	if i == nil {
    41→		return i
    42→	}
    43→	return &auditHandler{Interface: i}
    44→}

    17→package admission
    18→
    19→type Decorator interface {
    20→	Decorate(handler Interface, name string) Interface
    21→}
    22→
    23→type DecoratorFunc func(handler Interface, name string) Interface
    24→
    25→func (d DecoratorFunc) Decorate(handler Interface, name string) Interface {
    26→	return d(handler, name)
    27→}
    28→
    29→type Decorators []Decorator
    30→
    31→// Decorate applies the decorator in inside-out order, i.e. the first decorator in the slice is first applied to the given handler.
    32→func (d Decorators) Decorate(handler Interface, name string) Interface {
    33→	result := handler
    34→	for _, d := range d {
    35→		result = d.Decorate(result, name)
    36→	}
    37→
    38→	return result
    39→}
    40→

    18→
    19→type Decorator interface {
    20→	Decorate(handler Interface, name string) Interface
    21→}
    22→
    23→type DecoratorFunc func(handler Interface, name string) Interface
    24→
    25→func (d DecoratorFunc) Decorate(handler Interface, name string) Interface {
    26→	return d(handler, name)
    27→}
    28→
    29→type Decorators []Decorator
    30→
    31→// Decorate applies the decorator in inside-out order, i.e. the first decorator in the slice is first applied to the given handler.
    32→func (d Decorators) Decorate(handler Interface, name string) Interface {
    33→	result := handler
    34→	for _, d := range d {
    35→		result = d.Decorate(result, name)
    36→	}
    37→
    38→	return result
    39→}

Perfect! I've created the comprehensive answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary of Findings

I've identified **20 Go source files** that implement the Kubernetes API server admission controller pipeline, organized into these key categories:

### Core Admission Framework
- **interfaces.go**: Defines `Interface`, `MutationInterface`, and `ValidationInterface`
- **chain.go**: Implements `chainAdmissionHandler` with `Admit()` and `Validate()` methods for chain execution
- **plugins.go**: Orchestrates chain construction via `NewFromPlugins()`, registering and initializing plugins
- **reinvocation.go**: Wraps the chain to support webhook re-invocation when mutations occur
- **audit.go**: Adds audit logging via `WithAudit()` decorator

### Webhook Implementations
- **Mutating webhooks**: `plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go` and `dispatcher.go` handle object mutations via webhooks
- **Validating webhooks**: `plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go` and `dispatcher.go` validate objects without mutations
- **Generic webhook**: Shared base implementation and interfaces for both webhook types

### Configuration Management
- **mutating_webhook_manager.go** and **validating_webhook_manager.go**: Manage dynamic webhook configurations via Kubernetes informers
- **configuration_manager.go**: Base polling mechanism for configuration synchronization

### Kubernetes Integration
- **pkg/kubeapiserver/admission/**: Kubernetes-specific plugin initialization
- **pkg/controlplane/apiserver/admission/**: Controlplane-specific plugin initialization

The answer file includes the execution chain sequence: **NewFromPlugins → newReinvocationHandler → chainAdmissionHandler.Admit() → mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch() → chainAdmissionHandler.Validate() → validatingDispatcher.Dispatch()**

If no configuration is provided\n// the parameter is nil.\ntype Factory func(config io.Reader) (Interface, error)\n\ntype Plugins struct {\n\tlock     sync.Mutex\n\tregistry map[string]Factory\n}\n\nfunc NewPlugins() *Plugins {\n\treturn &Plugins{}\n}\n\n// All registered admission options.\nvar (\n\t// PluginEnabledFn checks whether a plugin is enabled.  By default, if you ask about it, it's enabled.\n\tPluginEnabledFn = func(name string, config io.Reader) bool {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n)\n\n// PluginEnabledFunc is a function type that can provide an external check on whether an admission plugin may be enabled\ntype PluginEnabledFunc func(name string, config io.Reader) bool\n\n// Registered enumerates the names of all registered plugins.\nfunc (ps *Plugins) Registered() []string {\n\tps.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer ps.lock.Unlock()\n\tkeys := []string{}\n\tfor k := range ps.registry {\n\t\tkeys = append(keys, k)\n\t}\n\tsort.Strings(keys)\n\treturn keys\n}\n\n// Register registers a plugin Factory by name. It returns `false` if\n// the name is not known. The error is returned only when the named provider was\n// known but failed to initialize.  The config parameter specifies the io.Reader\n// handler of the configuration file for the cloud provider, or nil for no configuration.\nfunc (ps *Plugins) getPlugin(name string, config io.Reader) (Interface, bool, error) {\n\tps.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer ps.lock.Unlock()\n\tf, found := ps.registry[name]\n\tif !found {\n\t\treturn nil, false, nil\n\t}\n\n\tconfig1, config2, err := splitStream(config)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, true, err\n\t}\n\tif !PluginEnabledFn(name, config1) {\n\t\treturn nil, true, nil\n\t}\n\n\tret, err := f(config2)\n\treturn ret, true, err\n}\n\n// splitStream reads the stream bytes and constructs two copies of it.\nfunc splitStream(config io.Reader) (io.Reader, io.Reader, error) {\n\tif config == nil || reflect.ValueOf(config).IsNil() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, nil\n\t}\n\n\tconfigBytes, err := io.ReadAll(config)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn bytes.NewBuffer(configBytes), bytes.NewBuffer(configBytes), nil\n}\n\n// NewFromPlugins returns an admission.Interface that will enforce admission control decisions of all\n// the given plugins.\nfunc (ps *Plugins) NewFromPlugins(pluginNames []string, configProvider ConfigProvider, pluginInitializer PluginInitializer, decorator Decorator) (Interface, error) {\n\thandlers := []Interface{}\n\tmutationPlugins := []string{}\n\tvalidationPlugins := []string{}\n\tfor _, pluginName := range pluginNames {\n\t\tpluginConfig, err := configProvider.ConfigFor(pluginName)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tplugin, err := ps.InitPlugin(pluginName, pluginConfig, pluginInitializer)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tif plugin != nil {\n\t\t\tif decorator != nil {\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, decorator.Decorate(plugin, pluginName))\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, plugin)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tif _, ok := plugin.(MutationInterface); If `get` is\n// successful, `Ready()` returns ready and `configuration()` returns the\n// `mergedConfiguration`; if `get` has failed more than `failureThreshold ` times,\n// `Ready()` returns not ready and `configuration()` returns nil configuration.\n// In an HA setup, the poller is consistent only if the `get` is\n// doing consistent read.\ntype poller struct {\n\t// a function to consistently read the latest configuration\n\tget getFunc\n\t// consistent read interval\n\t// read-only\n\tinterval time.Duration\n\t// if the number of consecutive read failure equals or exceeds the failureThreshold , the\n\t// configuration is regarded as not ready.\n\t// read-only\n\tfailureThreshold int\n\t// number of consecutive failures so far.\n\tfailures int\n\t// If the poller has passed the bootstrap phase. The poller is considered\n\t// bootstrapped either bootstrapGracePeriod after the first call of\n\t// configuration(), or when setConfigurationAndReady() is called, whichever\n\t// comes first.\n\tbootstrapped bool\n\t// configuration() retries bootstrapRetries times if poller is not bootstrapped\n\t// read-only\n\tbootstrapRetries int\n\t// Grace period for bootstrapping\n\t// read-only\n\tbootstrapGracePeriod time.Duration\n\tonce                 sync.Once\n\t// if the configuration is regarded as ready.\n\tready               bool\n\tmergedConfiguration runtime.Object\n\tlastErr             error\n\t// lock must be hold when reading/writing the data fields of poller.\n\tlock sync.RWMutex\n}\n\nfunc newPoller(get getFunc) *poller {\n\tp := poller{\n\t\tget:                  get,\n\t\tinterval:             defaultInterval,\n\t\tfailureThreshold:     defaultFailureThreshold,\n\t\tbootstrapRetries:     defaultBootstrapRetries,\n\t\tbootstrapGracePeriod: defaultBootstrapGraceperiod,\n\t}\n\treturn &p\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) lastError(err error) {\n\ta.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\ta.lastErr = err\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) notReady() {\n\ta.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\ta.ready = false\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) bootstrapping() {\n\t// bootstrapGracePeriod is read-only, so no lock is required\n\ttimer := time.NewTimer(a.bootstrapGracePeriod)\n\tgo func() {\n\t\tdefer timer.Stop()\n\t\t<-timer.C\n\t\ta.lock.Lock()\n\t\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\t\ta.bootstrapped = true\n\t}()\n}\n\n// If the poller is not bootstrapped yet, the configuration() gets a few chances\n// to retry. This hides transient failures during system startup.\nfunc (a *poller) configuration() (runtime.Object, error) {\n\ta.once.Do(a.bootstrapping)\n\ta.lock.RLock()\n\tdefer a.lock.RUnlock()\n\tretries := 1\n\tif !a.bootstrapped {\n\t\tretries = a.bootstrapRetries\n\t}\n\tfor count := 0; count < retries; count++ {\n\t\tif count > 0 {\n\t\t\ta.lock.RUnlock()\n\t\t\ttime.Sleep(a.interval)\n\t\t\ta.lock.RLock()\n\t\t}\n\t\tif a.ready {\n\t\t\treturn a.mergedConfiguration, nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif a.lastErr != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, a.lastErr\n\t}\n\treturn nil, ErrNotReady\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) setConfigurationAndReady(value runtime.Object) {\n\ta.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer a.lock.Unlock()\n\ta.bootstrapped = true\n\ta.mergedConfiguration = value\n\ta.ready = true\n\ta.lastErr = nil\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\n\tgo wait.Until(a.sync, a.interval, stopCh)\n}\n\nfunc (a *poller) sync() {\n\tconfiguration, err := a.get()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\ta.failures++\n\t\ta.lastError(err)\n\t\tif a.failures >= a.failureThreshold {\n\t\t\ta.notReady()\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\ta.failures = 0\n\ta.setConfigurationAndReady(configuration)\n}\n",

pipeline is implemented across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository, primarily in the staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver package. The architecture consists of three main layers: core admission interfaces, plugin implementations with webhook support, and request handler integration.\\n\\n## Core Admission Framework (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/)\\n\\nThe foundation is defined in interfaces.go, which declares three key interfaces:\\n- Interface: Base interface with a Handles(operation) method\\n- MutationInterface: Extends Interface, implements Admit(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for mutating admission\\n- ValidationInterface: Extends Interface, implements Validate(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) for validating admission\\n\\nThe chain.go file implements the actual admission chain execution through the chainAdmissionHandler type. It iterates through registered admission handlers, calling their Admit() methods for all MutationInterface implementations (lines 31-44), then Validate() methods for all ValidationInterface implementations (lines 47-60). The Handles() method (lines 63-70) enables filtering of operations.\\n\\nThe plugins.go file orchestrates chain construction via NewFromPlugins() (lines 127-163), which:\\n1. Iterates through enabled plugin names\\n2. Calls InitPlugin() to initialize each plugin with configuration\\n3. Wraps plugins with decorators (e.g., audit logging)\\n4. Constructs the chain handler from initialized plugins\\n5. Returns a wrapped chain via newReinvocationHandler() to support webhook re-invocation\\n\\nThe handler.go file provides the base Handler struct that manages supported operations via sets and a ReadyFunc for checking plugin readiness.\\n\\n## Chain Wrapping and Decoration\\n\\nThe reinvocation.go file wraps the chain handler to support webhook re-invocation policy. The reinvoker type (lines 27-29) calls Admit() twice if the reinvocation context indicates mutations occurred, allowing webhooks registered for re-invocation to be called again (lines 35-51).\\n\\nThe audit.go file adds audit logging via the WithAudit() decorator (line 39), which wraps the chain handler and logs admission annotations to audit events after Admit() and Validate() calls (lines 46-74).\\n\\nThe decorator.go file defines the Decorator interface for composing wrappers around admission handlers (lines 19-21), enabling inside-out application of decorators (line 32).\\n\\n## Webhook Implementation (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/)\\n\\nTwo webhook admission controller implementations exist:\\n\\n### Mutating Webhooks (plugin/webhook/mutating/)\\n- plugin.go: Defines the Plugin type implementing MutationInterface, registers as \\\"MutatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" (lines 28-76)\\n- dispatcher.go: Implements mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch() (lines 105-240) which:\\n  1. Retrieves mutating webhook configurations via webhook accessors\\n  2. Determines invocation eligibility based on resource selectors\\n  3. Calls each webhook via REST client\\n  4. Applies JSON patches to the object\\n  5. Tracks mutations for re-invocation\\n  6. Handles failure policies (Ignore vs Fail)\\n\\n### Validating Webhooks (plugin/webhook/validating/)\\n- plugin.go: Defines the Plugin type implementing ValidationInterface, registers as \\\"ValidatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" (lines 28-68)\\n- dispatcher.go: Implements validatingDispatcher.Dispatch() which:\\n  1. Retrieves validating webhook configurations\\n  2. Validates objects without mutations\\n  3. Supports parallel webhook invocation (unlike mutating)\\n  4. Handles rejections and audit annotations\\n\\nBoth use the generic webhook.go base implementation and interfaces.go Dispatcher interface.\\n\\n## Webhook Configuration Management (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/)\\n\\n- mutating_webhook_manager.go: NewMutatingWebhookConfigurationManager() creates a manager that lists MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects via informers (lines 53-89) and provides sorted webhook accessors with caching (lines 104-151)\\n- validating_webhook_manager.go: Analogous manager for ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects\\n- configuration_manager.go: Base polling mechanism for configuration synchronization\\n\\n## Kubernetes-Specific Initialization\\n\\n- pkg/kubeapiserver/admission/: Provides PluginInitializer for Kubernetes-specific plugins (WantsCloudConfig interface)\\n- pkg/controlplane/apiserver/admission/: Provides PluginInitializer for generic controlplane plugins (WantsQuotaConfiguration, WantsExcludedAdmissionResources interfaces)\\n\\n## Execution Flow\\n\\n1. **Startup**: NewFromPlugins() constructs the admission chain from enabled plugins, wraps with reinvocationHandler, wrapped with audit logging\\n2. **Request Processing**: API request handlers invoke the chain\\n3. **Mutating Phase**: chainAdmissionHandler.Admit() iterates handlers, calling Admit() on MutationInterface implementations\\n   - For webhooks: Plugin.Admit() delegates to mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n4. **Validating Phase**: chainAdmissionHandler.Validate() iterates handlers, calling Validate() on ValidationInterface implementations\\n   - For webhooks: Plugin.Validate() delegates to validatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n5. **Re-invocation**: If mutations occurred and re-invocation policy is set, the reinvoker calls Admit() again\\n6. **Audit Logging**: auditHandler.Admit/Validate() logs admission annotations to audit events\\n\\nThis architecture allows for:\\n- Extensible admission control via registered plugins\\n- Dynamic webhook configuration without API server restart\\n- Ordered, deterministic execution of admission phases\\n- Fine-grained failure policies per webhook\\n- Re-invocation of webhooks when mutations occur\\n- Audit trail of admission decisions\"\n}\n",
